{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-10-17 10:29:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-17 10:29:49","title":"FloorFound is bringing online return and resale to direct to consumer furniture businesses","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2061816","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Over the next five years consumers will return an estimated 40 million to 50 million pieces of furniture that more than likely will end up in landfills, creating tons of unnecessary waste, according to Chris Richter, the founder of a new Austin-based furniture startup, <a href=\"http://floorfound.com/\">FloorFound.</a></p>\n<p>To reduce that waste, and give retailers another option for their used goods, Richter has launched FloorFound. The company is designed to manage furniture returns and resale for online merchants. So far, companies like <a href=\"https://floydhome.com/\">Floyd Home</a>, <a href=\"https://insideweather.com/\">Inside Weather</a>, <a href=\"https://liveouter.com/\">Outer</a> and <a href=\"https://www.livefeather.com/\">Feather</a> (the furniture rental company) are using FloorFound&#8217;s services.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We have a very large pipeline and we&#8217;ve been operating since April first,&#8221; said Richter. &#8220;We can pick up in any major metro locally and inspect it locally. We have a platform layer where we can run inspections against those items.&#8221;</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>As consumers look to reduce their environmental footprint, an easy place to start is by buying used items, Richter said, and he expects that most brands will start to incorporate used and new products in their virtual and real showrooms. &#8220;Every brand will commingle new items with resale items,&#8221; he said. &#8220;We are trying to put retailers in the resale business with their own return inventory.&#8221; To prove his point, Richter pointed to companies like REI and <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/the-gap\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"the-gap\">The Gap, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <a href=\"https://www.retaildive.com/news/gap-latest-retailer-to-partner-with-thredup/572721/\">which have partnered with ThredUp to sell used clothes</a>.</p>\n<p>To complement its returns business and give online sellers a way to work more seamlessly with local vendors, the company has logistics partnerships with providers including Pilot Freight Services, Metropolitan Warehouse and Delivery and J.B. Hunt Transport.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Go5U07P6bc\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/05/13/minneapolis-based-yardbird-raised-4-4-million-for-furniture-made-from-recycled-ocean-bound-plastic/\">Minneapolis-based Yardbird raised $4.4 million for furniture made from recycled ocean-bound plastic</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Minneapolis-based Yardbird raised $4.4 million for furniture made from recycled ocean-bound plastic&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/05/13/minneapolis-based-yardbird-raised-4-4-million-for-furniture-made-from-recycled-ocean-bound-plastic/embed/#?secret=Go5U07P6bc\" data-secret=\"Go5U07P6bc\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Working with co-founder Ryan Matthews, the former director of technology for the Austin-based high-end retailer Kendra Scott, Richter has set up a business that can tap into both the demand for better customer service for the return of large items and the growing call for greater sustainability in the furniture industry.</p>\n<p>It was an attractive enough proposition to attract a pre-seed investment from Schematic Ventures, a venture fund focused exclusively on technological innovations for supply chain management.</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“The broken experience of oversized e-commerce has kept a multi-billion-dollar category offline. It&#8217;s not a simple problem: oversized items require coordination of a hyper-fragmented micro carrier network, complex physical processing, and then re-injection into an e-commerce channel that aligns with the brand,&#8221; said Julian Counihan, a general partner at Schematic Ventures. &#8220;UPS and FedEx just aren&#8217;t going to cut it. FloorFound is tackling this challenge with a team tailor-made for the task: Chris Richter, Ryan Matthews and Shannon Hardt have backgrounds spanning supply chain, delivery, e-commerce and enterprise software. FloorFound will be the final push that moves the remaining offline categories, online.</span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">” </span></i><i></i></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/oneplus\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"oneplus\">OnePlus <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> co-founder <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/carl-pei\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"carl-pei\">Carl Pei <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> has left the company, he confirmed on Friday. Pei, 31, said he plans to take some time off before pursuing his next step. &#8220;After nearly 7 years at OnePlus, I&#8217;ve made the difficult decision to say goodbye,&#8221; wrote Pei <a href=\"https://forums.oneplus.com/threads/thank-you.1323440/\">in a post</a> on the OnePlus forum.</p>\n<p>TechCrunch <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/12/carl-pei-leaves-oneplus/\">reported earlier this week</a> that Pei was leaving the company to start a new venture. Pei, who co-founded OnePlus in late 2013 with Pete Lau, has been the public face of the company ever since. He played an instrumental role in designing the OnePlus smartphone lineup over the years, and also how the company marketed them and itself.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"b1bWxcTplD\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/12/carl-pei-leaves-oneplus/\">OnePlus co-founder Carl Pei leaves the company to start a new venture</a></p></blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;OnePlus co-founder Carl Pei leaves the company to start a new venture&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/12/carl-pei-leaves-oneplus/embed/#?secret=b1bWxcTplD\" data-secret=\"b1bWxcTplD\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>“The world didn’t need another smartphone brand in 2013. But we saw ways of doing things better and dreamt of shaking things up. Better products. Built hand in hand with our users. At more reasonable prices. Fast forward to today, and OnePlus is a strong force to be reckoned when it comes to flagship smartphones. And the new Nord product line, this success will continue into new market segments,” Pei wrote in the post.</p>\n<p>Pei’s departure comes in the same week as OnePlus launched its new flagship smartphone, the OnePlus 8T. TechCrunch reached out to OnePlus for comment on Monday and has yet to hear back.</p>\n<p>News outlet Android Central <a href=\"https://www.androidcentral.com/confirmed-oneplus-co-founder-carl-pei-has-left-company\">speculated </a>earlier this week that Pei was leaving the firm possibly because of an alleged &#8220;internal power struggle&#8221; between him and Lau, 45. Lau took an additional role of SVP at Oppo. BBK Group owns OnePlus, Realme, Oppo and Vivo. OnePlus has always avoided questions about its ownership structure.</p>\n<p>“I am eternally grateful to Pete for taking a chance in this kid without a college degree, with nothing to his name but a dream. The trust, mentorship, and camaraderie will never be forgotten. Thanks for the opportunity of a lifetime,” Pei wrote.</p>\n<p>Pei said he was leaving the company because OnePlus had been his singular focus for the last seven years. &#8220;I&#8217;ve never regretted trusting my gut feeling, and this time it&#8217;s no different. These past years, OnePlus has been my singular focus, and everything else has had to take a backseat. I&#8217;m looking forward to taking some time off to decompress and catch up with my family and friends,&#8221; he wrote. &#8220;And then follow my heart on to what&#8217;s next.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"contributor-byline__more-articles\">\n\t\t<span class=\"more-articles-title\">More posts by this contributor</span>\n\t\t<ul class=\"more-articles-list\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<li><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/04/anthony-levandowski-sentenced-to-18-months-in-prison-as-new-4b-lawsuit-against-uber-is-filed/\">Anthony Levandowski sentenced to 18 months in prison as new $4B lawsuit against Uber is filed</a></li>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<li><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/09/the-risky-first-transatlantic-flight-of-a-reaper-drone/\">The risky first transatlantic flight of a Reaper drone</a></li>\n\t\t\t\t\t</ul>\n\t</div>\n\t</div>\n</div><p id=\"speakable-summary\">In pandemic-free years, America’s biggest trade show, CES, attracts more than 170,000 attendees, bringing traffic that jams surrounding roads day and night. To help absorb at least some of the congestion, the Las Vegas Convention Center (LVCC) last year planned a people-mover to serve an expanded campus. The LVCC wanted transit that could move up to 4,400 attendees every hour between exhibition halls and parking lots.</p>\n<p>It considered traditional light rail that could shuttle hundreds of attendees per train, but <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/03/06/elon-musk-boring-company-vegas-tunnel/\">settled on an underground system from Elon Musk’s The Boring Company</a> (TBC) instead &#8212; largely because Musk’s bid was tens of millions of dollars cheaper. The LVCC Loop would transport attendees through two 0.8-mile underground tunnels in Tesla vehicles, four or five at a time.</p>\n<p>But planning files reviewed by TechCrunch seem to show that the Loop system will not be able to move anywhere near the number of people LVCC wants, and that TBC agreed to.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Fire regulations peg the occupant capacity in the load and unload zones of one of the Loop’s three stations at just 800 passengers an hour. If the other stations have similar limitations, the system might only be able to transport 1,200 people an hour &#8212; around a quarter of its promised capacity.</p>\n<p>If TBC misses its performance target by such a margin, Musk’s company will not receive more than $13 million of its construction budget &#8212; and will face millions more in penalty charges once the system becomes operational.</p>\n<p>Neither TBC nor LVCVA responded to multiple requests for comment.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2061531\" style=\"width: 1002px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2061531\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2061531 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TBC-Vegas-NFPA-plan.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"992\" height=\"521\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TBC-Vegas-NFPA-plan.jpg 992w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TBC-Vegas-NFPA-plan.jpg?resize=150,79 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TBC-Vegas-NFPA-plan.jpg?resize=300,158 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TBC-Vegas-NFPA-plan.jpg?resize=768,403 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TBC-Vegas-NFPA-plan.jpg?resize=680,357 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TBC-Vegas-NFPA-plan.jpg?resize=50,26 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 992px) 100vw, 992px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2061531\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Fire regulations limit the load/unload zone near the cars to 800 people per hour. Credit: TBC/Clark County</p></div></p>\n<p>The LVCC always realized that it was taking a gamble on the Loop. Although Musk <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2017/10/28/heres-our-first-look-at-elon-musks-boring-co-la-tunnel/\">built a short demonstration tunnel near Los Angeles</a>, this would be the first public system with real customers and service requirements. An analysis by Las Vegas Mayor Carolyn Goodman in May 2019 concluded that TBC’s unproven system presented a high risk for the LVCC’s parent body, the Las Vegas Convention and Visitor’s Authority (LVCVA).</p>\n<p>So when the LCVCA wrote its contract with <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/the-boring-company\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"the-boring-company\">The Boring Company, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> it did its best to incentivize Musk to deliver on his promises. The contract would be for a fixed price, and TBC would have to hit specific milestones to receive all of its payments. When the bare tunnels are completed, which could happen any day now, TBC will have earned just over 30% of the total. The next big milestone is the completion of the entire working system, which would result in a pay-out of over $10 million.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"60oB2WPXcu\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/08/01/its-fight-night-in-las-vegas-elon-musks-loop-vs-the-monorail/\">It’s fight night in Las Vegas: Elon Musk’s Loop vs the Monorail</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;It’s fight night in Las Vegas: Elon Musk’s Loop vs the Monorail&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/08/01/its-fight-night-in-las-vegas-elon-musks-loop-vs-the-monorail/embed/#?secret=60oB2WPXcu\" data-secret=\"60oB2WPXcu\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>That was scheduled to have happened by October 1, so that the system would be ready for the next CES show in January. Although CES 2021 has now gone virtual and there is less time pressure on Musk to deliver, he presumably still wants to get paid.</p>\n<p>In a tweet this week, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/elon-musk\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"elon-musk\">Elon Musk <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> wrote that the system would be open in <a href=\"https://urldefense.proofpoint.com/v2/url?u=https-3A__twitter.com_elonmusk_status_1316301283234648064&#38;d=DwMFaQ&#38;c=sWW_bEwW_mLyN3Kx2v57Q8e-CRbmiT9yOhqES_g_wVY&#38;r=Bknt9owDQMbaeP0_bjaZeS2BjAU10Z9umfuqNXOTLSs&#38;m=cJRQNyQYkevEIsPyjsn6jp1T36acyN0uX5Q4nJ3o0jI&#38;s=EQ19lF6_0KLbduMQiu-vknGZ8q1Eth67lX_dpRLtoH4&#38;e=\">“maybe a month or so. Some finishing touches need to be done on the stations.”</a></p>\n<p>After another milestone for the completion of a test period and safety report, the system’s final three milestones relate to how many passengers it can carry. If the Loop can demonstrate moving 2,200 passengers an hour, TBC will get $4.4 million, then the same payment again for hitting 3,300, and the same again for 4,400 passengers an hour. Together, these capacity payments represent 30% of the fixed price contract.</p>\n<p>Even if TBC achieved those numbers during testing, the LVCVA was worried that it might not be able to maintain them once the system was operational, so it inserted yet another requirement: “[TBC] acknowledges liquidated damages are applicable for [TBC’s] failure to provide System Capacity for Full Facility Trade Show Events.”</p>\n<p>For each large trade show that TBC fails to transport an average capacity of 3,960 passengers per hour for 13 hours, it will have to pay LVCVA $300,000 in damages. If TBC keeps falling short, it keeps paying, up to a maximum of $4.5 million.</p>\n<p>So what is stopping TBC from transporting as many people as both it and the LVCC wants? There are national fire safety rules for underground transit systems that specify alarms, sprinklers, emergency exits and a maximum occupant load, to avoid overcrowding in the event of a fire.</p>\n<p>Building plans submitted by The Boring Company include a fire code analysis for one of the Loop’s above-ground stations:</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2061532\" style=\"width: 960px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2061532\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2061532 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TBC-Vegas-NFPA.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"950\" height=\"663\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TBC-Vegas-NFPA.jpg 950w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TBC-Vegas-NFPA.jpg?resize=150,105 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TBC-Vegas-NFPA.jpg?resize=300,209 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TBC-Vegas-NFPA.jpg?resize=768,536 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TBC-Vegas-NFPA.jpg?resize=680,475 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/TBC-Vegas-NFPA.jpg?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 950px) 100vw, 950px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2061532\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image source</strong>: The Boring Company/Clark County NV</p></div></p>\n<p>The above screenshot from the plans notes that the area where passengers get into and out of the <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/tesla-motors\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"tesla-motors\">Tesla <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> cars has a peak occupancy load of 100 people every 7.5 minutes, equivalent to 800 passengers an hour. Even if the other stations had higher limits, this would limit the system’s hourly capacity to about 1,200 people.</p>\n<p>“That sounds correct,” says Glenn Corbett, a professor of security, fire and emergency management at the John Jay College of Criminal Justice in New York. “But if that&#8217;s the bottleneck, the question from a safety standpoint is, what controls that [800 per hour]? Is it just pure honesty and people following the rules, or is there a mechanical thing that keeps them out?”</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The plans do not show any turnstiles or barriers to limit entry.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Even without the safety restrictions, the Loop may struggle to hit its capacity goals. Each of the 10 bays at the Loop’s stations must handle hundreds of passengers an hour, corresponding to perhaps 100 or more arrivals and departures, depending on how many people each car is carrying. That leaves little time to load and unload people and luggage, let alone make the 0.8-mile journey and occasionally recharge. </span></p>\n<p>[gallery ids=\"2061530,2061529,2061685,2061528\"]</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Although TBC’s </span><a href=\"https://www.lvloop.com/lvccloop\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Loop website</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> says that the system will use autonomous vehicles, a TBC executive told a planning committee last year that the cars would have human drivers “for additional safety.” TBC had proposed developing a larger capacity autonomous shuttle for the Loop, capable of carrying up to 16 people. The latest plans all show traditional sedans, however, and another Musk tweet this week admitted: <a href=\"https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/1316258179689443328\">“We simplified this a lot. It’s basically just Teslas in tunnels at this point.”</a></span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The most recent documents filed by TBC also show changes to the Loop’s original design. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Gone are striking curved roofs, with both aboveground stations now having flat photovoltaic canopies to help charge the Tesla vehicles. These terminal stations each have a single Supercharger station, and a “showpiece sculpture” consisting of a concrete segment similar to those used in the tunnels below. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The central, subterranean station has a large, open platform, and also houses the electrical, fire safety and IT equipment. Each station will have bays for 10 Tesla vehicles to load and unload passengers. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Even before the first Loop is operating, TBC is planning two more Loop tunnels nearby, connecting the LVCC to the Wynn Encore and Resorts World casinos. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The tunnel to the Encore is long enough that safety regulations require an emergency exit about halfway along. Plans indicate an emergency egress shaft and a small hatch, but it is unclear whether passengers escaping a fire or breakdown would be expected to climb stairs or even a ladder.</span></p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2061523\" style=\"width: 1431px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2061523\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2061523 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Loop-extension-egress.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1421\" height=\"800\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Loop-extension-egress.jpg 1421w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Loop-extension-egress.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Loop-extension-egress.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Loop-extension-egress.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Loop-extension-egress.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Loop-extension-egress.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1421px) 100vw, 1421px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2061523\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Loop extension egress. <strong>Image source:</strong> The Boring Company/Clark County NV</p></div></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">TBC last year suggested an emergency ladder for its proposed Loop between Baltimore and Washington, D.C., a system that Corbett called “</span><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/05/22/review-of-elon-musks-dc-to-baltimore-loop-system-reveals-safety-concerns/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">the definition of insanity</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">,” as it did not account for passengers with limited mobility. That project is now </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">on pause</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">TBC’s stated aim is to expand the LVCC Loop from a local people mover to a Vegas-wide transit system serving the Strip, the airport and eventually extending all the way to Los Angeles. If the company struggles to deliver capacity &#8212; and revenue &#8212; from its small-scale Convention Center system, the future of those ambitions could be in doubt. </span></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"cfNe6FbdZF\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/05/22/review-of-elon-musks-dc-to-baltimore-loop-system-reveals-safety-concerns/\">Review of Elon Musk&#8217;s DC-to-Baltimore &#8216;Loop&#8217; system reveals 10:29:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-17 10:29:49","title":"EU’s Google-Fitbit antitrust decision deadline pushed into 2021","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2061893","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The deadline for Europe to make a call on the <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/google\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"google\">Google <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a>-Fitbit merger has been pushed out again &#8212; with EU regulators now having until January 8, 2021, to take a decision.</p>\n<p>The latest change to the provisional deadline, spotted earlier by <a href=\"https://uk.reuters.com/article/us-fitbit-m-a-alphabet-eu/eu-antitrust-deadline-for-google-fitbit-deal-extended-to-jan-8-idUKKBN2711N2\">Reuters</a>, could be the result of one of the parties asking for more time.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/23/eus-antitrust-probe-of-google-fitbit-gets-more-time/\">Last month</a> the deadline for a decision was extended until December 23 &#8212; potentially pushing the decision out beyond a year after Google announced its intention to buy Fitbit, back in <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/11/01/google-is-acquiring-fitbit/\">November 2019</a>. So if the tech giant was hoping for a simple and swift regulatory rubberstamping its hopes have been diminishing since <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/04/google-fitbit-deal-to-be-scrutinized-in-europe-over-data-competition-concerns/\">August</a> when the Commission announced it was going to dig into the detail. <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2017/05/18/facebook-fined-122m-in-europe-over-misleading-whatsapp-filing/\">Once bitten and all that</a>.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The proposed <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/fitbit\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"fitbit\">Fitbit <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> acquisition also comes as Alphabet, Google&#8217;s parent, is under <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/09/09/forty-nine-states-and-the-district-of-columbia-are-pushing-an-antitrust-investigation-against-google/\">intense antitrust scrutiny</a> <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/28/how-to-watch-tech-hearing-antitrust/\">on multiple fronts</a> on home turf.</p>\n<p>Google featured prominently in a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/06/steps-from-the-house-judiciary-committee-are-too-little-too-late-when-it-comes-to-big-tech/\">report</a> by the House Judiciary Committee on big tech antitrust concerns earlier this month, with US lawmakers recommending a range of remedies &#8212; including breaking up platform giants.</p>\n<p>European lawmakers are also in the process of <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/30/europe-eyeing-limits-on-how-big-tech-can-use-data-and-bundle-apps-reports/\">drawing up new rules to regulate so-called &#8216;gatekeeper&#8217; platforms</a> &#8212; which would <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/04/google-pushes-europe-to-limit-gatekeeper-platform-rules/\">almost certainly apply to Google</a>. A legislative proposal on that is expected before the end of this year, which means it may appear before EU regulators have taken a decision on the Google-Fitbit deal. (And one imagines Google isn&#8217;t exactly stoked about that possibility.)</p>\n<p>Both <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/04/google-fitbit-deal-to-be-scrutinized-in-europe-over-data-competition-concerns/\">competition</a> and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/04/google-fitbit-deal-to-be-scrutinized-in-europe-over-data-competition-concerns/\">privacy</a> concerns have been raised against allowing Google get its hands on Fitbit users&#8217; data.</p>\n<p>The tech giant has responded by offering <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/29/google-offers-europe-more-checks-fitbit-data-wont-be-used-for-ads/\">a number of pledges to try to convince regulators</a> &#8212; saying it would not use Fitbit health and wellness data for ads and offering to have data separation requirements monitored. It has also said it would commit to maintain third parties&#8217;/rivals&#8217; access to its Android ecosystem and Fitbit&#8217;s APIs.</p>\n<p>However rival wearable makers have <a href=\"https://www.ft.com/content/d815b103-7d46-4dbe-b3c4-1d40d714b863\">continued to criticize the proposed merger</a>. And, earlier this week, consumer protection and human rights groups issued a <a href=\"https://edri.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/BEUC-X-2020-097-consumer-and-citizen-groups-continue-to-have-serious-concerns-about-Google-Fitbit-takeover.pdf\">joint letter</a> &#8212; urging regulators to only approve the takeover if &#8220;merger remedies can effectively prevent [competition and privacy] harms in the short and long term&#8221;.</p>\n<p>One thing is clear: With antitrust concerns now writ large against &#8216;big tech&#8217; the era of &#8216;friction-free&#8217; acquisitions looks to be behind Google et al.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"sXQNcq2fsC\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/07/big-tech-blows-a-collective-raspberry-at-the-houses-antitrust-report/\">Big tech blows a collective raspberry at the House&#8217;s antitrust report</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Big tech 10:29:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-17 10:29:49","title":"Lawmatics raises $2.5M to help lawyers market themselves","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2062104","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https://www.lawmatics.com\">Lawmatics</a>, a San Diego startup that&#8217;s building marketing and CRM software for lawyers, is announcing that it has raised $2.5 million in seed funding.</p>\n<p>CEO Matt Spiegel used to practice law himself, and he told me that even though tech companies have a wide range of marketing tools to choose from, “lawyers have not been able to adopt them,&#8221; because they need a product that’s tailored to their specific needs.</p>\n<p>That’s why Spiegel founded <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/lawmatics\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"lawmatics\">Lawmatics <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> with CTO Roey Chasman. He said that a law firm’s relationship with its clients can be divided into three phases — intake (when a client is deciding whether to hire a firm); the active legal case; and after the case has been resolved. Apparently most legal software is designed to handle phase two, while Lawmatics focuses on phases one and three.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The platform includes a CRM system to manage the initial client intake process, as well as tools that can automate a lot of what Spiegel called the “blocking and tackling” of marketing, like sending birthday messages to former clients — which might sound like a minor task, but Spiegel said it’s crucial for law firms to “nurture” those relationships, because most of their business comes from referrals.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"E4sJIDiWMm\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/07/thoughtriver-nabs-10m-to-speed-up-deal-making-with-ai-contract-review/\">ThoughtRiver nabs $10M to speed up deal-making with AI contract review</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;ThoughtRiver nabs $10M to speed up deal-making with AI contract review&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/07/thoughtriver-nabs-10m-to-speed-up-deal-making-with-ai-contract-review/embed/#?secret=E4sJIDiWMm\" data-secret=\"E4sJIDiWMm\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Lawmatics’ early adopters, Spiegel added, have consisted of the firms in areas where “if you need a lawyer, you go to Google and start searching ‘personal injury,’ ‘bankruptcy,’ ‘estate planning,’ all these consumer-driven law firms.” And the pandemic led to accelerated the startup&#8217;s growth, because “lawyers are at home now, their business is virtual and they need more tools.”</p>\n<p>Spiegel’s had success selling technology to lawyers in the past, with his practice management software startup MyCase<a href=\"https://www.appfolio.com/news/appfolio-acquires-mycase\"> acquired by AppFolio</a> in 2012 (AppFolio recently <a href=\"https://www.globenewswire.com/news-release/2020/09/08/2090127/0/en/AppFolio-Announces-Sale-of-MyCase-to-Funds-Advised-by-Apax-Partners.html\">sold MyCase to a variety of funds</a> for $193 million). He said that the strategies for growing both companies are “almost identical” — the products are different, but “it’s really the same segment, running the same playbook, only with additional go-to-market strategies.”</p>\n<p>The funding was led by <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/eniac-ventures\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"eniac-ventures\">Eniac Ventures <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and Forefront Venture Partners, with participation from Revel Ventures and Bridge Venture Partners.</p>\n<p>“In my 10 years investing I have witnessed few teams more passionate, determined, and capable of revolutionizing an industry,” said Eniac’s Tim Young in a statement. “They have not only created the best software product the legal market has seen, they have created a movement.”</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"mhw7rkshCW\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/03/atrium-shuts-down/\">$75M legal startup Atrium shuts down, lays off 100</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"contributor-byline__bio\">\n\t\tJason Chuang is a researcher at Mozilla.\t</div>\n\t\n\t</div>\n</div><p id=\"speakable-summary\">Dear Mr. Zuckerberg, Mr. Dorsey, Mr. Pichai and Mr. Spiegel: We need universal digital ad transparency now!</p>\n<p>The negative social impacts of discriminatory ad targeting and delivery are well-known, as are the social costs of disinformation and exploitative ad content. The prevalence of these harms has been demonstrated repeatedly by our research. At the same time, the vast majority of digital advertisers are responsible actors who are only seeking to connect with their customers and grow their businesses.</p>\n<p>Many advertising platforms acknowledge the seriousness of the problems with digital ads, but they have taken different approaches to confronting those problems. While we believe that platforms need to continue to strengthen their vetting procedures for advertisers and ads, it is clear that this is not a problem advertising platforms can solve by themselves, as they themselves acknowledge. The vetting being done by the platforms alone is not working; public transparency of all ads, including ad spend and targeting information, is needed so that advertisers can be held accountable when they mislead or manipulate users.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Our research has shown:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Advertising platform system design allows advertisers to discriminate against users based on their gender, race and other sensitive attributes.</li>\n<li>Platform ad delivery optimization can be discriminatory, regardless of whether advertisers attempt to set inclusive ad audience preferences.</li>\n<li>Ad delivery algorithms may be causing polarization and make it difficult for political campaigns to reach voters with diverse political views.</li>\n<li>Sponsors spent more than $1.3 billion dollars on digital political ads, yet disclosure is vastly inadequate. Current voluntary archives do not prevent intentional or accidental deception of users.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>While it doesn’t take the place of strong policies and rigorous enforcement, we believe transparency of ad content, targeting and delivery can effectively mitigate many of the potential harms of digital ads. Many of the largest advertising platforms agree; <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/facebook\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"facebook\">Facebook, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> Google, Twitter and Snapchat all have some form of an ad archive. The problem is that many of these archives are incomplete, poorly implemented, hard to access by researchers and have very different formats and modes of access. We propose a new standard for universal ad disclosure that should be met by every platform that publishes digital ads. If all platforms commit to the universal ad transparency standard we propose, it will mean a level playing field for platforms and advertisers, data for researchers and a safer internet for everyone.</p>\n<p>The public deserves full transparency of all digital advertising. We want to acknowledge that what we propose will be a major undertaking for platforms and advertisers. However, we believe that the social harms currently being borne by users everywhere vastly outweigh the burden universal ad transparency would place on ad platforms and advertisers. Users deserve real transparency about all ads they are bombarded with every day. We have created a detailed description of what data should be made transparent that you can find <a href=\"https://onlinepoliticaltransparencyproject.org/universal-digital-ad-transparency-required-fields/\">here</a>.</p>\n<p>We researchers stand ready to do our part. The time for universal ad transparency is now.</p>\n<p>Signed by:</p>\n<p>Jason Chuang, Mozilla<br />\nKate Dommett, University of Sheffield<br />\nLaura Edelson, New York University<br />\nErika Franklin Fowler, Wesleyan University<br />\nMichael Franz, Bowdoin College<br />\nArchon Fung, Harvard University<br />\nSheila Krumholz, Center for Responsive Politics<br />\nBen Lyons, University of Utah<br />\nGregory Martin, Stanford University<br />\nBrendan Nyhan, Dartmouth College<br />\nNate Persily, Stanford University<br />\nTravis Ridout, Washington State University<br />\nKathleen Searles, Louisiana State University<br />\nRebekah Tromble, George Washington University<br />\nAbby Wood, University of Southern California</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote is serious about transparency, let’s open-source our SDKs</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;If the ad Thompson","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn67@2020_5/2020/10/17/02-29-56-919_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn4@2020_6/2020/10/17/02-30-04-663_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn55@2020_6/2020/10/17/02-30-03-551_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=ktwtguRSr7k:-fjL7xh330w:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn98@2020_3/2020/10/17/02-30-15-193_f956887f8a614f21.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=ktwtguRSr7k:-fjL7xh330w:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn83@2020_4/2020/10/17/02-30-04-499_e0b296bdfb811428.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn32@2020_4/2020/10/17/02-30-05-019_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/ktwtguRSr7k":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn6@2020_1/2020/10/17/02-30-03-465_7e057e52079fd0cc.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602901789465},{"createdTime":"2020-10-17 10:29:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-17 10:29:49","title":"Datto sets initial IPO price range, indicating a valuation of around $4B","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2061890","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">It was just a few weeks ago that <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/datto\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"datto\">Datto, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/30/vista-owned-backup-and-recovery-company-datto-files-to-go-public/\">what TechCrunch called a</a> &#8220;backup and disaster recovery firm,&#8221; filed to go public. This week the firm set an initial range for its debut.</p>\n<p>The <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/vista-equity-partners\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"vista-equity-partners\">Vista Equity Partners <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a>-backed company was picked up by the private equity firm back in 2017. Vista is back in the news lately for several reasons, some stemming from <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/vista-equity-s-smith-reaches-settlement-with-doj-in-tax-probe-11602713545\">executive shenanigans</a> &#8212; read: <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-10-15/billionaire-robert-smith-admits-he-cheated-on-taxes-for-15-years?sref=gni836kR\">tax evasion and huge penalties</a> &#8212; but at least what&#8217;s coming from Datto&#8217;s camp is good tidings.</p>\n<p>How so? Vista bought Datto for <a href=\"https://www.crn.com/news/channel-programs/datto-confidentially-files-to-launch-ipo-bloomberg\">around $1.5 billion</a>, and is set to make billions on its exit, based on the company&#8217;s expected IPO pricing.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Per the data firm&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1724570/000119312520268957/d36878ds1a.htm\">latest S-1 filing</a>, Datto is targeting a $24 to $27 per share price range. Here&#8217;s the math:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Total shares outstanding after IPO, sans underwriters&#8217; allotment: 157,548,740 shares</li>\n<li>Total shares outstanding after IPO, with underwriters&#8217; allotment: 160,848,740</li>\n<li>Max valuation at current prices, sans underwriters&#8217; allotment: $4.25 billion</li>\n<li>Max valuation at current prices, with underwriters&#8217; allotment: $4.34 billion</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Those two final numbers are dramatically bigger than the $1.5 billion that Vista is said to have paid for Datto.</p>\n<p>How has Datto managed to generate so much value in the last few years? In financial terms, the company grew to a run rate of around $500 million, based on its Q1 and Q2 2020 revenue results. That gives the company a revenue multiple of less than 10x at its current IPO price maximum.</p>\n<p>And that price makes sense. Datto is not growing very quickly, just 16% from H1 2019 to H1 2020, for example. The company did recently become profitable, however, which helps its valuation case. But more importantly, between 2017 and 2020 we have seen revenue multiples for software companies expand. That, plus Datto&#8217;s growth since 2017, have repriced it far above its sale price.</p>\n<p>For Vista, it&#8217;s good news. Provided that they don&#8217;t get into tax issues over this particular set of returns. More on Datto as it prices and debuts.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"TRxDd1V1CN\"><p><a src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/OFKzgbeV9_Q\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 16 Oct 2020 15:43:47 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI","linkMd5":"37a899a70f085004afc4a3b2ec8aa865","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn67@2020_5/2020/10/17/02-29-56-919_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","destWidth":59,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":990,"destBytes":324,"author":"Alex Wilhelm","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn67@2020_5/2020/10/17/02-29-56-919_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn4@2020_6/2020/10/17/02-30-04-663_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn55@2020_6/2020/10/17/02-30-03-551_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=OFKzgbeV9_Q:QFbwFjBN2fY:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn27@2020_1/2020/10/17/02-30-05-003_100e8be4851891cd.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=OFKzgbeV9_Q:QFbwFjBN2fY:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn43@2020_2/2020/10/17/02-30-04-375_c461ce61262dbf62.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn32@2020_4/2020/10/17/02-30-05-019_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/OFKzgbeV9_Q":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn96@2020_5/2020/10/17/02-30-04-617_f0e0adfd8c1e361e.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602901789466},{"createdTime":"2020-10-17 10:29:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-17 10:29:49","title":"Crypto-driven marketplace Zora raises $2M to build a sustainable creator economy","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2061692","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Dee Goens and Jacob Horne have both the exact and precisely opposite background that you’d expect to see from two people building a way for creators to build a sustainable economy for their followers to participate in. Coinbase, crypto-hack projects at university, KPMG, Merrill Lynch. But where’s the art?</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“Believe it or not, I used to have dreams of being a rapper,” laughs Goens. “There’s a SoundcCloud out there somewhere. With that passion you explore the inner workings of the music industry. I would excitedly ask industry friends about the advance and 360 deal models only to realize they were completely broken.”</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">And, while many may be well-intentioned, these deal structures often exploit artistry. In many cases taking the majority of an artist&#8217;s ownership. &#8220;I grew curious why artists were unable to resource themselves from their community in an impactful way &#8212; but instead, were forced to seek out potentially predatory relationships. To me, this was bullshit.&#8221;</span></p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Horne says that he’d always wanted to create a fashion brand. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“I always thought a fashion brand would be something I’d do after crypto,” he tells me. “I love crypto but it felt overly focused on just finance and felt like it was missing something. Then I started to play with the idea of combining these two passions and starting Saint Fame.”</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While at Coinbase, Horne hacked on </span><a href=\"https://www.saintfame.com/fame\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Saint Fame</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, a side project that leveraged some of the ideas on display in Zora. It was a marketplace that allowed people to sell and trade items with cryptocurrency, buying intermediate variable-value tokens redeemable for future goods. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“I realized that culture itself was shaped and built upon an old financial system that is systemically skewed against artists and communities,” says Horne. “The operating system of ownership was built in the 1600s with the Dutch East India Trading Company and early Nation States. Like what the fuck is up with that?” </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">We have the internet now, we can literally create and share information to billions of people all at once, and the ownership system is the same as when people had to get on a boat for six months to send a letter. It’s time for an upgrade. Any community on the internet should be able to come together, with capital, and work towards any shared vision. That starts with empowering creators and artists to create and own the culture they’re creating. In the long term this moves to internet communities taking on societal endeavors.”</span></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"6ZKlB2LDOQ\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/16/the-cryptocurrency-moment/\">The cryptocurrency moment</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;The cryptocurrency moment&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/16/the-cryptocurrency-moment/embed/#?secret=6ZKlB2LDOQ\" data-secret=\"6ZKlB2LDOQ\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The answer that they’re working on is called <a href=\"https://ourzora.com/\">Zora</a>. It’s a marketplace with two main components but one philosophy: sustainable economics for creators. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">All too often creators are involved in reaping the rewards for their work only once, but the secondary economy continues to generate value out of their reach. Think of an artist, as an example, that creates a piece and sells it for market value. That’s great, but thereafter, every ounce of work that the artist puts into future work, into building a name and a brand and a community for themselves puts additional value into that piece. The artist never sees a dime from that, relying instead on the value of future releases to pay dividends on the work. </span></p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2061698\" style=\"width: 2286px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2061698\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2061698 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.27.23-PM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"2276\" height=\"2276\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.27.23-PM.png 2276w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.27.23-PM.png?resize=150,150 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.27.23-PM.png?resize=300,300 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.27.23-PM.png?resize=768,768 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.27.23-PM.png?resize=680,680 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.27.23-PM.png?resize=1536,1536 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.27.23-PM.png?resize=2048,2048 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.27.23-PM.png?resize=32,32 32w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.27.23-PM.png?resize=50,50 50w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.27.23-PM.png?resize=64,64 64w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.27.23-PM.png?resize=96,96 96w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.27.23-PM.png?resize=128,128 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 2276px) 100vw, 2276px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2061698\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits: Zora</p></div></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">That’s basically the way it has always worked. I have a little background in this as I used to exhibit and was involved in running a gallery and my father is a fine artist. If he sells a painting today for $300, gets a lot better, more popular and more valued over time, the owner of that painting may re-sell it for hundreds or thousands more. He will never see a dime of that. And God forbid that an artist like him gets too locked into the gallery system, which slices off enormous chunks of the value of a piece for a square of wall space and the marketing cachet of a curator or storefront. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The same story can be told across the recording industry, fashion, sports and even social media. Lots of middle-people and lots of vigs to pay. And, unsurprisingly, the same creators of color that drive so much of The Culture are the biggest losers, hands down. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The primary Zora product is a market that allows creators or artists to launch products and then continue to participate in their second market value. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Here’s how the Zora team explains it:</span></p>\n<blockquote><p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">On Zora, creators have the ability to set two prices: start price and max price. As community members buy and sell a token, it moves the price up or down. This makes the price dynamic as it opens price discovery on the items by the market. When people buy the token it moves the price closer to its maximum. When they sell, it moves closer to its minimum. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">For an excited community like Jeff [Staple’s], this new dynamic price can cause a quick increase in the value of his sneakers. As a creator, they capture the value from selling on a price curve as well as getting a take on trading fees from the market which they now own. What used to trade on StockX is now about to trade on a creator owned market.</span></p></blockquote>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There have been some early successes. Designer and marketer Jeff Staple launched a run of 30 </span><a href=\"https://ourzora.com/reverse-land/reverse?variant=95\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Coca-Cola x Staple SB Dunk customs</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> by Reverseland and their value is trending up around 234% since release. A Benji Taylor x Kevin Doan </span><a href=\"https://ourzora.com/benjixkevin/toy\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">vinyl figure is up 210%</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I have seen some other stabs at this. When he was still at <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/stockx/\">StockX</a>, founder Josh Luber launched their </span><a href=\"https://stockx.com/news/new-balance-no-vacancy-inn-ipo-recap/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Initial Product Offerings</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, a Blind Dutch Auction system that allowed the market to set a price for an item, with some of the cut of pricing above market going back to the manufacturer or brand making the offering. The focus there was brands versus individual creators (though they did launch with a Ben Baller slide). Allowing brands to tap into second market value for limited goods is a lot less of a revolution play, but the thesis is similar. I thought that was a good idea then, and I like it even better when it’s being used to democratize rather than maximize returns. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Side note: I love that this team is messing around with interesting ideas like dogfooding their own marketplace with the value of being in their own TestFlight group. I’m sort of like, </span><a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aF1qQxPhybE\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">is that allowed</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, but at the same time it’s dope and I’ve never seen anything like it. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Zora was founded in May of 2020 (right in the middle of this current panny-palooza). The team is Goens (Creators and Community), Horne (Product), Slava Kim (Design), Dai Hovey (Engineering), Ethan Daya (Engineering) and Tyson Battistella (Engineering). </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Zora has raised a $2 million seed round led by Kindred Ventures, with participation from Trevor McFedries of Brud, Alice Lloyd George, Jeff Staple, Coinbase Ventures and others.</span></p>\n<h2>Tokenized community</h2>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">But this idea that physical goods or even digitally packaged works have to exist as finite containers of value is not a given either. Goens and Horne are pushing to challenge that too with the first big new product for Zora: community tokens. Built on Ethereum, </span><a href=\"https://blog.ourzora.com/introducing-rac\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">the $RAC token</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> is the first of its kind from Zora. André Allen Anjos, stage name RAC, is a Portuguese-American musician and producer who makes remixes that stream on the web, original music and has had commercial work featured in major brand ads. </span></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"sBbViTBeE4\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/06/10/crypto-startup-school-how-to-build-companies-by-building-communities/\">Crypto Startup School: How to build companies by building communities    </a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Crypto Startup School: How to build companies by building communities    &#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/06/10/crypto-startup-school-how-to-build-companies-by-building-communities/embed/#?secret=sBbViTBeE4\" data-secret=\"sBbViTBeE4\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Though he is popular and has a following in the tens of thousands, RAC is not a social media superpower. The token distribution and subsequent activity in trades and sales is purely driven by the buy-in that his fans feel. This is a key learning for a lot of players in this new economy: raw numbers are the social media equivalent of a billboard that people drive by. It may get you eyeballs, but it doesn’t guarantee action. The modern creator is living in a house with their fans, offering them access and interacting via Discord and Snap and comments. </span></p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2061697\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2061697\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2061697 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.30.49-PM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"777\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.30.49-PM.png 2284w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.30.49-PM.png?resize=150,114 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.30.49-PM.png?resize=300,227 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.30.49-PM.png?resize=768,582 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.30.49-PM.png?resize=680,516 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.30.49-PM.png?resize=1536,1165 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.30.49-PM.png?resize=2048,1553 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-15-at-3.30.49-PM.png?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2061697\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image Credits: Zora</p></div></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">But those houses are all other people’s houses, which leads into the reason that Zora is launching a token.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The token drop serves multiple purposes: </span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><b>It unites fans across multiple silos. </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Whether they’re on Intsa, TikTok, Spotify or Snapchat, they can all earn tokens. That token serves as a unifying community unit of value that they all understand and pivot around. It’s a way to own a finite binary “atom” of an artist’s digital being.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><b>It creates a pool of value that an artist can own and distribute themselves.</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Currently you cannot buy $RAC directly. You can only earn it. Some of that is retroactive for loyal supporters. If, for instance, you followed RAC on Bandcamp dating back to 2009, you’ll get some of a pool of 25,000 RAC. Bought a bit of RAC merch? You get some credit in tokens too. Future RAC distributions will be given to Patron supporters, merch purchasers, etc.</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><b>The value stays in the artist&#8217;s universe, rather than being spun out into currency.</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> It serves as a way for the artist to incentivize, reward and energize their followers. RAC fans who buy his mixtape get tokens, and they can redeem them for purchases of further merch. </span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><b>It allows more flexibility for creators whose work doesn’t fall so neatly into package-able categories.</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Performance art, activism, bite-sized entertainment. These are not easy to &#8220;drop&#8221; for money. But if you have a circulating token that grows in value as you grow your audience, there is definitely something there. </span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The future of Zora most immediately involves spinning up a self-service version of the marketplace, allowing creators and entrepreneurs to launch their products without a direct partnership and onboarding. There are many, many uncertainties here and the team has a lot of challenges ahead on the traction and messaging front. But as mentioned, some early releases have shown promise, and the philosophy is sound and much needed. As the creator universe/passion economy/whatever you call it depends on how old you are/fandom merchant wave rises, there is definitely an opportunity to rethink how the value of their contributions are assigned and whether there is a way to turn the long-term labor of building a community into long-term value. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The last traded price of RAC’s tape, BOY, by the way? </span><a href=\"https://ourzora.com/rac/tape\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">$3,713</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, up 18,465%. </span></p>\n<div id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/twitter\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"twitter\">Twitter <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> has taken another step back from its initial decision to block users from sharing links to or images of a New York Post story reporting on emails and other data supposedly originating on a laptop belonging to Democratic presidential nominee Joe Biden&#8217;s son, Hunter.</p>\n<p>The story, which alleged that Hunter Biden had set up a meeting between a Ukrainian energy firm and his father back when Biden was vice president, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/14/suspect-provenance-of-hunter-biden-data-cache-prompts-skepticism-and-social-media-bans/\">looked shaky from the start</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.thedailybeast.com/man-who-reportedly-gave-hunters-laptop-to-rudy-speaks-out-in-bizarre-interview\">more</a> <a href=\"https://twitter.com/spdustin/status/1316621229751762945\">holes</a> have emerged over time. Both Facebook and Twitter took action to slow its spread — but Twitter seemed to take the more aggressive stance, not just limiting reach but actually blocking links.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"1KyArFDChH\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/16/twitter-changes-its-hacked-materials-policy-in-wake-of-new-york-post-controversy/\">Twitter changes its hacked materials policy in wake of New York Post controversy</a></p></blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Twitter changes its hacked materials policy in wake of New York Post controversy&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/16/twitter-changes-its-hacked-materials-policy-in-wake-of-new-york-post-controversy/embed/#?secret=1KyArFDChH\" data-secret=\"1KyArFDChH\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>These moves have drawn a range of criticism. There have been predictable cries of censorship from Republican politicians and pundits, but there have also been suggestions that <a href=\"https://www.theverge.com/2020/10/15/21516729/facebook-twitter-new-york-post-hunter-biden-emails-laptop-story-social-media-moderation-problems\">Facebook and Twitter inadvertently drew more attention to the story</a>. And even Twitter&#8217;s CEO Jack Dorsey suggested that it was &#8220;unacceptable&#8221; to block links in DMs without an explanation.</p>\n<p>Casey Newton, on the other hand, argued that the platforms had <a href=\"https://www.platformer.news/p/youtube-comes-for-q\">successfully slowed the story&#8217;s spread</a>: &#8220;The truth had time to put its shoes on before Rudy Giuliani’s shaggy-dog story about a laptop of dubious origin made it all the way around the world.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Twitter initially justified its approach by citing its hacked materials policy, then later said it was blocking the Post article for including &#8220;personal and private information — like email addresses and phone numbers — which violate our rules.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The controversy did prompt Twitter to <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/16/twitter-changes-its-hacked-materials-policy-in-wake-of-new-york-post-controversy/\">revise its hacked materials policy</a>, so that content and links obtained through dubious means will now come with a label, rather than being removed entirely, unless it&#8217;s being shared directly by hackers or those &#8220;acting in concert with them.&#8221;</p>\n<p>And now, as <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/10/16/technology/twitter-new-york-post.html\">first reported by The New York Times</a>, Twitter is also allowing users to share links to the Post story itself (something I&#8217;ve confirmed through my own Twitter account).</p>\n<p>Why the reversal? Again, the official justification for blocking the link was to prevent the spread of private information, so the company said that the story has now spread so widely, online and in the press, that the information can no longer be considered private.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"nff0PGMiHT\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/14/suspect-provenance-of-hunter-biden-data-cache-prompts-skepticism-and-social-media-bans/\">Suspect provenance of Hunter Biden data cache prompts skepticism and social media bans</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Suspect provenance of Hunter Biden data cache prompts
