+0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI","linkMd5":"5a80cac526d6ace2cd88469ffb98ad12","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn67@2020_5/2020/10/17/02-29-56-919_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","destWidth":59,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":990,"destBytes":324,"author":"Anthony Ha","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn67@2020_5/2020/10/17/02-29-56-919_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn4@2020_6/2020/10/17/02-30-04-663_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn55@2020_6/2020/10/17/02-30-03-551_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=BTeNYaq6ynk:NuCItuU0VlI:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn12@2020_3/2020/10/17/02-30-04-730_ab3ba587cd6235ec.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=BTeNYaq6ynk:NuCItuU0VlI:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn2@2020_5/2020/10/17/02-30-03-568_1e5273b31b3e8972.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn32@2020_4/2020/10/17/02-30-05-019_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/BTeNYaq6ynk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn68@2020_3/2020/10/17/02-30-05-486_6cc8eaba7f973a8f.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602901789467},{"createdTime":"2020-10-17 10:29:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-17 10:29:49","title":"The need for true equity in equity compensation","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2059382","description":"<div class=\"article__contributor-byline-wrapper\">\n<div class=\"article__contributor-byline\">\n\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__contributor\">\n\t\t<div class=\"byline__author\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class=\"byline__author-name\">Carine Schneider</span>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<span class=\"byline__author-title\" style=\"display: block;\">Contributor</span>\n\t\t</div>\n\n\t\t\t\t<div class=\"contributor__twitter\">\n\t\t\t<a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://twitter.com/carineschneider\">\n\t\t\t\t\t<svg class=\"icon icon--twitter icon--white\" viewBox=\"0 0 20 20\" version=\"1.1\" aria-labelledby=\"title\">\n\t\t<title>Share on Twitter</title>\n\t\t<path d=\"M20,4c-0.7,0.3-1.5,0.6-2.4,0.7c0.9-0.5,1.5-1.4,1.8-2.3c-0.8,0.5-1.7,0.8-2.6,1C16.1,2.5,15,2,13.8,2c-2.3,0-4.1,1.9-4.1,4.2c0,0.3,0,0.7,0.1,1C6.4,7,3.4,5.4,1.4,2.9C1,3.5,0.8,4.1,0.8,4.9c0,1.4,0.7,2.7,1.8,3.5C2,8.4,1.4,8.2,0.8,7.9v0.1c0,2,1.4,3.7,3.3,4.1c-0.4,0.1-0.7,0.2-1.1,0.2c-0.3,0-0.5,0-0.8-0.1c0.5,1.7,2,2.9,3.8,2.9c-1.4,1.1-3.2,2-5.1,2c-0.3,0-0.7,0-1-0.1c1.8,1.2,4,1.7,6.3,1.7c7.5,0,11.7-6.4,11.7-12V6.1C18.8,5.6,19.4,4.8,20,4z\"/>\t</svg>\n\t\t\t\t</a>\n\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\n\t\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__bio\">\n\t\tCarine Schneider is the president of <a href=\"https://astrella.com/\">AST Private Company Solutions, Inc.</a>, a division of <a href=\"https://www.astfinancial.com/\">AST Financial.</a>\t</div>\n\t\n\t</div>\n</div><p id=\"speakable-summary\">I began my career at <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/oracle\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"oracle\">Oracle <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> in the mid-1980s and have since been around the proverbial block, particularly in Silicon Valley working for and with companies ranging from the Fortune 50 to global consulting companies to leading a number of startups, including <a href=\"https://astrella.com/\">the SaaS company I presently lead</a>. Throughout my career, I’ve carved out a niche not only working with technology companies, but focused on designing and implementing global compensation programs.</p>\n<p>In short, if there’s two things I know like the back of my hand, it’s tech and how people are paid.</p>\n<p>The compensation evolution I’ve witnessed over these past 35+ years has been dramatic. Among other things, there has been a fundamentally seismic shift in how women are perceived and paid, principally for the better. Some of it, in truth, has been window dressing. It’s good PR to say you’re a company with a strong culture focused on diversity, as it helps attract top talent. But the rubber meets the road once hires get past the recruiter. When companies don’t do what they say, we see mass exoduses and even lawsuits, as has recently been the case at <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/11/former-coo-sues-pinterest-accusing-it-of-gender-discrimination-retaliation-and-wrongful-termination/\">Pinterest</a> and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/30/do-option-grants-create-gender-and-racial-inequity/\">Carta</a>.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>So with the likes of Intel, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/salesforce\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"salesforce\">Salesforce <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and Apple publicly committed to gender pay equity, there’s nothing left to see here, right? Actually, we’re not even close. Yes, the glass ceiling is cracking. But significant, largely unaddressed gaps remain relative to the broader scope of long-tail compensation for women, especially at startups, where essential measures of economic reward such as stock options in companies are often not even part of the conversation around pay parity.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"O0W1okFS9u\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/11/former-coo-sues-pinterest-accusing-it-of-gender-discrimination-retaliation-and-wrongful-termination/\">Former COO sues Pinterest, accusing it of gender discrimination, retaliation and wrongful termination</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Former COO sues Pinterest, accusing it of gender discrimination, retaliation and wrongful termination&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/11/former-coo-sues-pinterest-accusing-it-of-gender-discrimination-retaliation-and-wrongful-termination/embed/#?secret=O0W1okFS9u\" data-secret=\"O0W1okFS9u\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>As a baseline, while progress is evident, gender pay is an unfinished product to say the least. Recently the <a href=\"https://www.bls.gov/news.release/pdf/wkyeng.pdf\">U.S. Bureau of Labor Statistics found</a> white women earn 83.3% as much as their white male counterparts, while African-American women earn 93.7% compared to men of their same race. Asian women made 77.1% and Hispanic women earned 85.1% as much respectively.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.payscale.com/data/gender-pay-gap\">According to Payscale</a>, the ratio of the median earnings of women to men has decreased by just $0.07 since 2015, and in 2020, women make $0.81 for every dollar a man makes. Long term, in calculating presumptive raises given over a 40-year career, women could lose as much as $900,000 over the duration of a career.</p>\n<p>But that’s just the tip of the iceberg. Even if we solely left the gender pay gap to just a cash salary disparity, there <em>is</em> something further to see here. However, to quote a famous pitchman, “But wait, there’s more!” And the <em>more</em> — at least in my mind — is far more troubling.</p>\n<p>As innovative startups from Silicon Valley to New York’s Silicon Alley and beyond continue to reshape the business landscape, guess how most of them are able to lure bright, entrepreneurial minds? It’s certainly not salary, as when a company has nothing beyond a great idea and maybe a lead to a VC on Sand Hill Road, there’s no fat paycheck or benefits package to offer. Instead, they dangle the proverbial carrot of stock/equity compensation.</p>\n<p>“Look, we know you can get $180,000 a year from <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/apple\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"apple\">Apple <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> but we’ll give you $48,000 a year plus 1,000 shares presently valuated at $62 per share. Our board — which is packed with studs from the Bay Area — is expecting that to soar within two years! Wait ‘til we go public!”</p>\n<p>This is the pitch, at least if you’re a promising <em>male</em>. But <em>women</em>, historically, have tended to get left out of this lucrative reward package for varying reasons.</p>\n<p>How has this happened? Beyond just a furtherance of business culture, while there have been legislative steps taken to address inequities in public company compensation and stock dispersal, there are no regulations as to how private companies distribute or manage the appreciation of stock. And, as we all know, the appreciation can be potentially massive.</p>\n<p>It makes sense. Many companies and even naïve job-seekers consider equity as the “third pillar” of compensation beyond titles/compensation (which come hand-in-hand) and benefits. Shares of startups are just not top-of-mind — often ignored or misunderstood — by many who look at gender pay inequities, although that could not be more misguided.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://psycnet.apa.org/buy/2020-51967-001\">A recent study </a>published in the &#8220;Journal of Applied Psychology&#8221; found a gender gap for equity-based awards ranging from 15%-30% — even beyond accounting for typical reasons women historically earn less than men, including differences in occupation and length of service at a company. Keep in mind many of these companies will go on to massive valuations, and for some, lucrative IPOs or acquisitions.</p>\n<p>It’s a problem I recognized long ago, and it is largely why I agreed to lead our Bay Area startup on behalf of our New York-based parent company <a href=\"http://astfinancial.com\">AST</a>. I found a commitment to a genuinely equitable culture instilled by a shared moral compass, a belief that companies who care about gender equity perform better and provide better returns, and a conviction that diversity brings unique perspectives, drives talent retention, builds a stronger culture and aids client satisfaction.</p>\n<p>In speaking with industry colleagues, I know it’s something CEOs, both men and women, are dedicated to addressing. I believe creating a broader picture of compensation is essential for startups, global conglomerates and every company in between. If you are in a position of leadership and recognize this is a challenge in need of addressing at your company, here are some steps I recommend you implement:</p>\n<ol>\n<li><strong>Look at the data: </strong>Do the analysis. See if this is truly an issue at your company, and if it is, commit to creating a level playing field. There are plenty of experienced consultants who can help you work through remediation strategies.</li>\n<li><strong>Remove subjectivity:</strong> Hire an independent arbiter to analyze your data, as it removes the politics and emotion, as well as bias from the work product.</li>\n<li><strong>Create compensation bands:</strong> Much like the government’s GS system, create a salary grade system that contains bands of compensation for specific roles. Prior to hiring a person, decide which band the job responsibilities should be assigned.</li>\n<li><strong>Empower a champion:</strong> Identify and empower an internal champion to truly own parity — someone whose performance is judged based upon creating equity company-wide. Instead of assigning it to your human resources chief, create a chief diversity officer role to own it. After all, this is bigger than just pay or medical benefits. This is the culture and thus foundation of your company.</li>\n<li><strong>Get your board on board:</strong> Educate your board as to why this matters. If your board doesn’t value this, it ultimately won’t matter. Companies have audit committee chairs or nominations chairs. Identify a &#8220;culture chair.&#8221;</li>\n</ol>\n<p>One of the first reports we created is <a href=\"https://astrella.com/product/\">a Pay Comparison Report</a> so there are tools anyone in management can easily use to review stock grants made to all employees and ensure equity between people of different ethnicities or gender. It’s not that hard if you care to look.</p>\n<p>When I was graduating from college and Ronald Reagan was in office, we were talking about the potential for women to break the glass ceiling. Now, many years later, somehow we’ve managed to develop lights you can turn on and off by clapping and most of us are walking around with the power of a supercomputer in our hands. Is it really asking too much that we require gender pay equity, including all three compensation pillars (cash, benefits and stock), to be a priority?</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"dcq34akLlh\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/30/do-option-grants-create-gender-and-racial-inequity/\">Are option grants promoting gender and racial inequity?</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Are option grants promoting gender and racial 10:29:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-17 10:29:49","title":"Human Capital: Prop 22 puts the ‘future of labor’ at stake","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2061648","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Welcome back to Human Capital, where we look at the latest in tech labor and diversity and inclusion.</p>\n<p>Because election day is quickly approaching and given that California&#8217;s Prop 22 puts the &#8220;future of labor&#8221; at stake, as Instacart worker and co-organizer at Gig Workers Collective Vanessa Bain told TechCrunch this week, we&#8217;re paying close attention to this ballot measure. Gig companies like Uber, Lyft, DoorDash and Instacart have put more than $180 million into Prop 22, which seeks to keep their drivers and delivery workers classified as independent contractors.</p>\n<p>Before we jump in, friendly reminder that Human Capital will soon be a newsletter&#8230;starting next week! <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/newsletters\">Sign up here</a> so you don&#8217;t miss it.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<hr />\n<h2 style=\"text-align: center;\"><b>Gig Work</b></h2>\n<hr />\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><strong>Instacart began asking workers to pass out Yes on Prop 22 propaganda to customers</strong></span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Vanessa Bain, Instacart shopper and co-founder of Gig Workers Collective, tweeted about how some shoppers were instructed to pass out Yes on 22 stickers to customers. The inserts and stickers were available at a store in the Bay Area over the weekend, but Instacart says there are no plans to expand that to other stores.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Many people, including Bain, questioned whether it was legal or not. </span></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Unbelievable. <a href=\"https://twitter.com/Instacart?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@Instacart</a> is now requiring Shoppers to do the uncompensated work of distributing Prop 22 propaganda to customers —against our own self-interests. Even *if* (big if) this is legal, it is reprehensible and establishes a dangerous precedent for workers. <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/NOonProp22?src=hash&#38;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#NOonProp22</a> <a href=\"https://t.co/NXVblutvsh\">pic.twitter.com/NXVblutvsh</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; Vanessa Bain <img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.0.0/72x72/270a.png\" alt=\"✊\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.0.0/72x72/2764.png\" alt=\"❤\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.0.0/72x72/1f6d2.png\" alt=\"🛒\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /> #BlackLivesMatter #NOonProp22 (@hashtagmolotov) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtagmolotov/status/1315073745006989312?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">October 10, 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></div>\n<p>Instacart, however, <a href=\"https://amp.cnn.com/cnn/2020/10/13/tech/proposition-22-instacart/index.html?__twitter_impression=true\">told CNN the initiative was allowed under campaign finance rules</a>. Additionally, <span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I reached out to the Fair Political Practices Commission, but was told by Communications Director Jay Wierenga that “only an investigation by FPPC Enforcement (or a DA or the AG’s Office) determines whether someone or group violated the Political Reform Act.” </span></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"w5ls7pePug\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/06/im-a-software-engineer-at-uber-im-voting-against-prop-22/\">I’m a software engineer at Uber and I’m voting against Prop 22</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;I’m a software engineer at Uber and I’m voting against Prop 22&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/06/im-a-software-engineer-at-uber-im-voting-against-prop-22/embed/#?secret=w5ls7pePug\" data-secret=\"w5ls7pePug\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">What is clear, however, is that it goes against what many workers want. </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">We actually caught up with Bain ahead of the relaunch of <a href=\"https://podcasts.apple.com/us/podcast/techcrunch-mixtape/id1317432118\">TechCrunch Mixtape</a>, where she discussed why she’s anti Prop 22. The episode goes live next week, but here’s a bit of a teaser from our conversation:</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“The future of labor is at stake,” Bain told us earlier this week. “I would argue the future of our democracy, as well. The reality is that, you know, it establishes a dangerous precedent to allow companies to write their own labor laws&#8230;This policy was created to unilaterally benefit companies at the detriment of workers.”</span></p>\n<p><strong>Hundreds took to SF&#8217;s streets in protest of Prop 22</strong></p>\n<p>In San Francisco, there was a massive protest against Prop 22. While Prop 22 would provide more benefits than workers currently have, many drivers and delivery workers say that&#8217;s not enough. For example, Prop 22 would institute healthcare subsidies, but it falls short of complete healthcare.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Y’all there are hundreds of people here, starting our drivers caravan outside Uber’s HQ.</p>\n<p>We’re all demanding <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/NoOnProp22?src=hash&#38;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#NoOnProp22</a>.</p>\n<p>Drivers deserve living wages, healthcare, &#38; benefits.</p>\n<p>We’re gonna fight to get them. <a href=\"https://t.co/EEVZcVRKqX\">pic.twitter.com/EEVZcVRKqX</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; Gig Workers Are Voting No On Prop 22 (@GigWorkersRise) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/GigWorkersRise/status/1316819743207157761?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">October 15, 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></div>\n<p><strong>Speaking of SF, 76% of app-based workers in the city are people of color</strong></p>\n<p>And 39% are immigrants, according to the latest survey of gig workers conducted by the Local Agency Formation Commission and UC Santa Cruz Professor Chris Benner.</p>\n<p>This study surveyed 259 workers who drive or deliver for DoorDash, Instacart or Amazon Fresh. Other findings were:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>71% of workers get at least 3/4 of monthly income from gig work</li>\n<li>57% of workers completely rely on gig work for their monthly income</li>\n<li>On average, workers make $450 per week. After expenses, that averages drops to $270 per week.</li>\n</ul>\n<p><strong>California appeals court heard arguments in the Uber, Lyft gig worker classification case</strong></p>\n<p>California 1st District Court of Appeal judges heard arguments from Uber and Lyft about why they should be able to continue classifying their drivers as independent contractors. The hearing was a result of a district judge granting a preliminary injunction that would force Uber and Lyft to immediately reclassify their workers as employees. Uber and Lyft, however, appealed the ruling and now here we are.</p>\n<p>As Uber and Lyft have argued drivers would lose flexibility if forced to be employees, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/kateconger/status/1316072368343666690\">an appeals court judge asked what part of AB 5 would require companies to take away that flexibility</a>. Spoiler alert: there&#8217;s nothing in AB 5 that requires such a thing.</p>\n<p>But a lawyer for Lyft, which has said it would leave California if forced to reclassify its workers, <a href=\"https://scvnews.com/uber-lyft-lobby-california-appeals-court-to-keep-drivers-as-contractors/\">said he doesn&#8217;t</a> &#8220;want the court to think that if the injunction is affirmed, that these people will continue to have these earnings opportunities because they won&#8217;t.&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Uber&#8217;s survey of workers on Prop 22 shows strong support for the ballot measure</strong></p>\n<p>But it&#8217;s important to note that of the more than 200,000 Uber drivers in California, only 461 workers participated in the study. Uber conducted this survey from September 23 through October 5 to see how drivers felt about Prop 22 and being an independent contractor. In that survey, 54% of respondents said they would definitely vote yes on 22 if the election were today while 13% said they would definitely vote no.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2062053\" style=\"width: 619px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2062053\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2062053\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-16-at-10.45.04-AM.png?w=609\" alt=\"\" width=\"609\" height=\"231\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-16-at-10.45.04-AM.png 609w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-16-at-10.45.04-AM.png?resize=150,57 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-16-at-10.45.04-AM.png?resize=300,114 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-16-at-10.45.04-AM.png?resize=50,19 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 609px) 100vw, 609px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2062053\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Uber</p></div></p>\n<p>Those surveyed also weighed in on whether they prefer to be independent contractors; 54% of those surveyed said they strongly prefer being an independent contractor while 9% said they strongly prefer being an employee.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2062062\" style=\"width: 550px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2062062\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2062062\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-16-at-10.51.47-AM.png?w=540\" alt=\"\" width=\"540\" height=\"240\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-16-at-10.51.47-AM.png 540w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-16-at-10.51.47-AM.png?resize=150,67 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-16-at-10.51.47-AM.png?resize=300,133 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Screen-Shot-2020-10-16-at-10.51.47-AM.png?resize=50,22 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 540px) 100vw, 540px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2062062\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Uber</p></div></p>\n<p>This week, Uber also encouraged riders to talk to their drivers about Prop 22 to see how they feel about it.</p>\n<p>&#8220;First and foremost, the conversation about Proposition 22 should be about what gig workers actually want,&#8221; an Uber spokesperson said in a statement. &#8220;That’s why we are encouraging everyone who uses Uber or Uber Eats to ask their driver or delivery person how they really feel about Prop 22.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Based on the wording of the in-app message, Uber seems confident most drivers do support Prop 22.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2062059\" style=\"width: 324px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2062059\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical wp-image-2062059 size-large\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1.png?w=314\" alt=\"\" width=\"314\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1.png 750w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1.png?resize=69,150 69w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1.png?resize=139,300 139w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1.png?resize=314,680 314w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1.png?resize=709,1536 709w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/1.png?resize=23,50 23w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 314px) 100vw, 314px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2062059\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits: </strong>Uber</p></div></p>\n<hr />\n<h2 style=\"text-align: center;\"><b>Stay woke</b></h2>\n<hr />\n<p><b>Facebook and Twitter ban Holocaust-denial posts </b></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Both </span><a href=\"https://about.fb.com/news/2020/10/removing-holocaust-denial-content/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Facebook</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> and Twitter took a step in their ongoing battles against hate this week by removing posts that deny the Holocaust, the systematic and state-sponsored mass murder of around 6 million Jewish people. On Monday, Facebook announced it would block posts that deny the Holocaust. Facebook said its decision was driven by the rise in anti-Semitism and “the alarming level of ignorance about the Holocaust, especially among young people.” On Wednesday, </span><a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-10-14/twitter-like-facebook-to-remove-posts-denying-the-holocaust?sref=ctSjKj2N\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Twitter announced a similar stance.</span></a></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"24S3ydsdxf\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/12/facebook-in-a-reversal-will-now-ban-holocaust-denial-content-under-its-hate-speech-policy/\">Facebook, in a reversal, will now ban Holocaust denial content under its hate-speech policy</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Facebook, in a reversal, will now ban Holocaust denial content under its hate-speech policy&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/12/facebook-in-a-reversal-will-now-ban-holocaust-denial-content-under-its-hate-speech-policy/embed/#?secret=24S3ydsdxf\" data-secret=\"24S3ydsdxf\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p><b>BLCK VC launches Black Venture Institute</b></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In partnership with Operator Collective, Salesforce Ventures and UC Berkeley Haas School of Business, </span><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/blck-vc-launches-educational-initiative-to-bring-more-blacks-into-investing-ecosystem/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">BLCK VC’s Black Venture Institute</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> wants to help more Black entrepreneurs become angel investors. The goal is to train 300 students over the next three years to be in a position of writing checks. </span></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"smO97sgiQF\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/blck-vc-launches-educational-initiative-to-bring-more-blacks-into-investing-ecosystem/\">BLCK VC launches educational initiative to bring more Black entrepreneurs into investing ecosystem</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;BLCK VC launches educational initiative to bring more Black entrepreneurs into investing ecosystem&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/13/blck-vc-launches-educational-initiative-to-bring-more-blacks-into-investing-ecosystem/embed/#?secret=smO97sgiQF\" data-secret=\"smO97sgiQF\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“It is these closed networks that have helped contribute to the lack of access for the Black community over the years,” BLCK VC co-founder Frederik Groce told TC’s Ron Miller. “Black Venture Institute is a structural attempt to create access for Black operators — from engineers to product marketing managers.”</span></p>\n<p><b>GV finally has a Black female partner, Terri Burns</b></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Terri Burns recently made partner at GV, formerly known as Google Ventures. Burns is now the only Black female partner at GV, which is wild. But, you know, progress, not perfection. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Throwback to when Burns spoke a bit about racial justice in tech and venture capital. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“Venture capital certainly plays a role,” Burns, then a principal at GV, told TechCrunch about the overall lack of diversity in tech. “VC is a tool that can enable businesses to scale greatly and quickly, and historically, this tool hasn’t been equally distributed. For example, VC has traditionally focused on founders from a small number of institutions and pedigrees that are not particularly diverse (in 2016 we learned from Richard Kerby, general partner at Equal Ventures, that 40% of VCs went to either Harvard or Stanford). With more equal distribution of funds across backgrounds, underrepresented people will have a greater chance at success.”</span></p>\n<p><b>The Wing co-founder admits her mistakes </b></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Audrey Gelman, the former CEO of The Wing who resigned in June,</span><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/14/the-wing-co-founder-apology/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> posted a letter she sent to former employees of The Wing last week</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. In it, Gelman apologized for not taking action to combat mistreatment of women of color at The Wing. She also acknowledged that her drive for success and scaling quickly “came at the expense of a healthy and sustainable culture that matched our projected values, and workplace practices that made our team feel valued and respected.”</span></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ejjYy51GmD\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/14/the-wing-co-founder-apology/\">The Wing co-founder admits the co-working space upheld &#8216;the kind of social inequality we set out to upend&#8217;</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;The Wing co-founder admits the co-working space upheld &#8216;the kind of social inequality we set out to upend&#8217;&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/14/the-wing-co-founder-apology/embed/#?secret=ejjYy51GmD\" data-secret=\"ejjYy51GmD\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">That meant, Gelman said, The Wing “had not subverted the historical oppression and racist roots of the hospitality industry; we had dressed it up as a kindler [sic], gentler version.”</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Here are some other highlights from her letter:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“Members’ needs came first, and those members were often white, and affluent enough to afford The Wing’s membership dues.”</span></li>\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“White privilege and power trips were rewarded with acquiescence, as opposed to us doubling down on our projected values.”</span></li>\n<li><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“When the realization set in that The Wing wasn’t institutionally different in the ways it had proclaimed, it hurt more because the space we claimed was different reinforced the age-old patterns of women of color and especially Black women being disappointed by white women and our limited feminist values.”</span></span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><em>Human Capital launches as a newsletter next Friday. <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/newsletters\">Sign up here</a> to get this delivered 10:29:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-17 10:29:49","title":"Private equity firms can offer enterprise startups a viable exit option","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2061899","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Four years ago, <a href=\"https://www.pingidentity.com/\">Ping Identity</a> was at a crossroads. A venerable player in the single sign-on market, its product was <a href=\"https://www.okta.com/resources/idaas-leader-gartner-magic-quadrant/TechGenix/\">not a market leader</a>, and after 14 years and $128 million in venture capital, it needed to find a new path.</p>\n<p>While the company had<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2015/10/13/ping-identity-opens-up-about-its-financials-as-it-eyes-2017-ipo/\"> once discussed an IPO</a>, by 2016 it began putting out feelers for buyers. Vista Equity Partners <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2016/06/12/ping-shapes-new-identity-after-600-million-acquisition/\">made a $600 million offer</a> and promised to keep building the company, something that corporate buyers wouldn&#8217;t guarantee. Ping CEO and co-founder Andre Durand accepted Vista&#8217;s offer, seeing it as a way to pay off his investors and employees and exit the right way. Even better, his company wasn&#8217;t subsumed into a large entity as likely would have happened with a typical M&#38;A transaction.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"tyy2W2nlWB\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2015/10/13/ping-identity-opens-up-about-its-financials-as-it-eyes-2017-ipo/\">Ping Identity Opens Up About Its Financials As It Eyes 2017 IPO</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Ping Identity Opens Up About Its Financials As It Eyes 2017 IPO&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2015/10/13/ping-identity-opens-up-about-its-financials-as-it-eyes-2017-ipo/embed/#?secret=tyy2W2nlWB\" data-secret=\"tyy2W2nlWB\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>As it turned out, the IPO-or-acquisition question wasn&#8217;t an either/or proposition. Vista continued to invest in the company, using small acquisitions <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2016/08/02/ping-identity-expands-mission-to-customers-with-unboundid-acquisition/\">like UnboundID</a> and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/06/26/ping-identity-acquires-stealthy-api-security-startup-elastic-beam/\">Elastic Beam</a> to fill in its roadmap, and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/08/23/ping-identity-files-for-100m-ipo/\">Ping went public last year</a>. The company’s experience shows that private equity offers a reasonable way for mature enterprise startups with decent but not exceptional growth &#8212; like the 100% or more venture firms tend to favor &#8212; to exit, pay off investors, reward employees and still keep building the company.</p>\n<p>But not everyone that goes this route has a tidy outcome like Ping&#8217;s. Some companies get brought into the P/E universe where they replace the executive team, endure big layoffs or sell off profitable pieces and stop investing in the product. But the three private equity firms we spoke to &#8212; Vista Equity, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/thoma-bravo\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"thoma-bravo\">Thoma Bravo <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and Scaleworks &#8212; all wanted to see their acquisitions succeed, even if they each go about it differently.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"isXF3z41sv\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2016/06/12/ping-shapes-new-identity-after-600-million-acquisition/\">Ping shapes new identity after $600 million acquisition</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Ping shapes new identity after $600 million acquisition&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2016/06/12/ping-shapes-new-identity-after-600-million-acquisition/embed/#?secret=isXF3z41sv\" data-secret=\"isXF3z41sv\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<h2>Viable companies with good numbers</h2>\n<p><div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=xlYbyc__Hzk:glqUd7Ad1lY:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=xlYbyc__Hzk:glqUd7Ad1lY:7Q72WNTAKBA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=xlYbyc__Hzk:glqUd7Ad1lY:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=xlYbyc__Hzk:glqUd7Ad1lY:-BTjWOF_DHI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=xlYbyc__Hzk:glqUd7Ad1lY:-BTjWOF_DHI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=xlYbyc__Hzk:glqUd7Ad1lY:D7DqB2pKExk\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=xlYbyc__Hzk:glqUd7Ad1lY:D7DqB2pKExk\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=xlYbyc__Hzk:glqUd7Ad1lY:qj6IDK7rITs\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/xlYbyc__Hzk\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 16 Oct 2020 18:11:46 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI","linkMd5":"4de5aac2cfab42838cd27583181f66f2","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn67@2020_5/2020/10/17/02-29-56-919_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","destWidth":59,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":990,"destBytes":324,"author":"Ron Miller","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn67@2020_5/2020/10/17/02-29-56-919_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn4@2020_6/2020/10/17/02-30-04-663_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn55@2020_6/2020/10/17/02-30-03-551_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=xlYbyc__Hzk:glqUd7Ad1lY:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn79@2020_1/2020/10/17/02-30-03-562_d5b22f09a324d203.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=xlYbyc__Hzk:glqUd7Ad1lY:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn1@2020_2/2020/10/17/02-30-03-484_a9f9ec2614277ebc.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn32@2020_4/2020/10/17/02-30-05-019_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/xlYbyc__Hzk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn86@2020_1/2020/10/17/02-30-03-574_3b4fcac53e6fcedd.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602901789456},{"createdTime":"2020-10-17 10:29:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-17 10:29:49","title":"IAB Europe’s ad tracking consent framework found to fail GDPR standard","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2061800","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">A flagship framework for gathering Internet users&#8217; consent for targeting with behavioral ads &#8212; which is designed by ad industry body, the IAB Europe &#8212; fails to meet the required legal standards of data protection, according to findings by its EU data supervisor.</p>\n<p>The Belgian DPA&#8217;s investigation follows complaints against the use of personal data in the real-time bidding (RTB) component of programmatic advertising which contend that a system of high velocity personal data trading is inherently incompatible with data security requirements baked into EU law.</p>\n<p>The IAB Europe&#8217;s Transparency and Consent Framework (TCF) can be seen popping up all over the regional web, asking users to accept (or reject) ad trackers &#8212; with the stated aim of helping publishers comply with the EU&#8217;s data protection rules.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>It was the ad industry standard&#8217;s body&#8217;s response to a major update to the bloc&#8217;s data protection rules, after the General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR) came into application in May 2018 &#8212; tightening standards around consent to process personal data and introducing supersized penalties for non-compliance &#8212; thereby cranking up the legal risk for the ad tracking industry.</p>\n<p>The IAB Europe introduced the TCF in <a href=\"https://iabeurope.eu/knowledgehub/policy/introducing-for-public-comment-transparency-and-consent-framework-tcf-version-2-0/#:~:text=IAB%20Europe%20launched%20its%20Transparency,the%20GDPR%20and%20ePrivacy%20Directive.\">April 2018</a>, saying at the time that it would &#8220;help the digital advertising ecosystem comply with obligations under the GDPR and ePrivacy Directive&#8221;.</p>\n<p>The framework has been widely adopted, including by adtech giant, Google &#8212; which integrated it this August.</p>\n<p>Beyond Europe, the IAB has also recently been pushing for a version of the same tool to be used for &#8216;compliance&#8217; with <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/01/01/the-california-consumer-privacy-act-officially-takes-effect-today/\">California&#8217;s Consumer Privacy Act</a>.</p>\n<p>However the findings by the investigatory division of the Belgian data protection agency cast doubt on all that adoption &#8212; suggesting the framework is not fit for purpose.</p>\n<p>The inspection service of the Belgium DPA makes a number of findings in a report reviewed by TechCrunch &#8212; including that the TCF fails to comply with GDPR principles of transparency, fairness and accountability, and also the lawfulness of processing.</p>\n<p>It also finds that the TCF does not provide adequate rules for the processing of special category data (e.g. health information, political affiliation, sexual orientation etc) &#8212; yet <em>does</em> process that data.</p>\n<p>There are further highly embarrassing findings for the IAB Europe, which the inspectorate found not to have appointed a Data Protection Officer, nor to have a register of its own internal data processing activities.</p>\n<p>Its own <a href=\"https://iabeurope.eu/privacy-policy/\">privacy policy</a> was also found wanting.</p>\n<p>We&#8217;ve reached out to the IAB Europe for comment on the inspectorate&#8217;s findings. <strong>Update: </strong>See the base of this article for a first response. <strong>Update 2:</strong> The ad standards body has now published a statement <a href=\"https://iabeurope.eu/news-blog/iab-europe-comments-on-belgian-dpa-report/\">here</a> in which it describes the TCF as a &#8220;voluntary standard&#8221; that contains &#8220;a minimal set of best practices&#8221;. It also says it &#8220;respectfully disagree[s] with the [Belgian DPA]’s apparent interpretation of the law, pursuant to which IAB Europe is a data controller in the context of publishers’ implementation of the TCF&#8221;, adding: &#8220;If upheld, the [Belgian DPA]’s interpretation would have a chilling effect on the development of open-source compliance standards that serve to support industry players and protect consumers.&#8221;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/05/20/gdpr-adtech-complaints-keep-stacking-up-in-europe/\">A series of complaints against RTB have been filed across Europe</a> over the past two years, starting in the UK and Ireland.</p>\n<p>Dr Johnny Ryan, who filed the original RTB complaints &#8212; and is now a senior fellow at the <a href=\"https://www.iccl.ie/news/gdpr-watchdogs-investigation-finds-that-tracking-and-consent-pop-ups-used-by-google-and-other-major-websites-and-apps-are-unlawful/\">Irish Council for Civil Liberties</a> &#8212; told TechCrunch: &#8220;The TCF was an attempt by the tracking industry to put a veneer or quasi-legality over the massive data breach at the heart of the behavioral advertising and tracking industry and the Belgian DPA is now peeling that veneer off and exposing the illegality.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Ryan has previously described the RTB issues as “the greatest data breach ever recorded”.</p>\n<p>Last month he published another <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/21/irelands-data-watchdog-slammed-for-letting-adtech-carry-on-biggest-breach-of-all-time/\">hair-raising dossier of evidence</a> on how extensively and troublingly RTB leaks personal data &#8212; with findings including that a data broker used RTB to profile people with the aim of influencing the 2019 Polish Parliamentary Election by targeting LGBTQ+ people. Another data broker was found to be profiling and targeting Internet users in Ireland under categories including “Substance abuse”, “Diabetes,” “Chronic Pain” and “Sleep Disorders”.</p>\n<p>In a statement, Ravi Naik, the solicitor who worked on the original RTB complaints, had this to say on the Belgian inspectorate&#8217;s findings: “These findings are damning and overdue. As the standard setters, the IAB is responsible for breaches of the GDPR. Their supervisory authority has rightly found that the IAB &#8216;neglects&#8217; the risks to data subjects. The IAB’s responsibility now is to stop these breaches.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Following the filing of RTB complaints, the UK&#8217;s data watchdog, the ICO, issued a warning about behavioural advertising in <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/06/20/behavioural-advertising-is-out-of-control-warns-uk-watchdog/\">June 2019</a> &#8212; urging the industry to take note of the need to comply with data protection standards.</p>\n<p>However the regulator has failed to follow up with any enforcement action &#8212; unless you count multiple <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/01/17/privacy-experts-slam-uks-disastrous-failure-to-tackle-unlawful-adtech/\">mildly worded blog posts</a>. Most recently it <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/05/07/adtech-scores-a-pandemic-pause-from-uk-privacy-oversight/\">paused its (still ongoing) investigation into the issue</a> because of the pandemic.</p>\n<p>In another development last year, Ireland&#8217;s DPC <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/05/22/googles-lead-eu-regulator-opens-formal-privacy-probe-of-its-adtech/\">opened an investigation</a> into Google&#8217;s online Ad Exchange &#8212; looking into the lawful basis for its processing of personal data. But that investigation is one of <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/02/19/lack-of-big-tech-gdpr-decisions-looms-large-in-eu-watchdogs-annual-report/\">scores that remain open on its desk</a>. And the Irish regulator continues to <a href=\"https://twitter.com/maxschrems/status/1317137890330202112\">face criticism</a> over the length of time it&#8217;s taking to issue decisions on major cross-border GDPR cases pertaining to big tech.</p>\n<p>Jef Ausloos, a postdoc researcher in data privacy at the University of Amsterdam &#8212; and one of the complainants in the Belgian case &#8212; told TechCrunch the move by the DPA puts pressure on other EU regulators to act, calling out what he described as &#8220;<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/01/17/privacy-experts-slam-uks-disastrous-failure-to-tackle-unlawful-adtech/\">their complete, deer-in-the-headlights inaction</a>&#8220;.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I think we&#8217;ll see more of this in the coming months/year, i.e. other DPAs sick and tired, taking matters into their own hands &#8212; instead of waiting on the Irish,&#8221; he added.</p>\n<p>“We are happy to finally see a data protection authority having the resolved to take on the online advertisement industry at its roots. This may be the first important step in taking down surveillance capitalism,&#8221; Ausloos also said in a statement.</p>\n<p>There are still several steps to go before the Belgian DPA takes (any) action on the substance of its inspectorate&#8217;s report &#8212; with a number of steps outstanding in the regulatory process. We&#8217;ve reached out to the Belgian DPA for comment. <strong>Update</strong>: See below.</p>\n<p>But, per the complainants, the inspectorate&#8217;s findings have been forwarded to the Litigation Chamber, and action is expected in early 2021. Which suggests privacy watchers in the EU might finally get to uphold their rights against the ad tracking industry/<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/11/19/a-10-point-plan-to-reboot-the-data-industrial-complex-for-the-common-good/\">data industrial complex</a> in the near future.</p>\n<p>For publishers the message is a need to change <em>how</em> they monetize their content: Rights-respecting alternatives to creepy ads are possible (e.g. contextual ad targeting which does not use personal data). <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/24/data-from-dutch-public-broadcaster-shows-the-value-of-ditching-creepy-ads/\">Some publishers</a> have already found the switch to contextual ads to be a good news story for their revenues. Subscription business models are also available (even if <a href=\"https://twitter.com/roelofbotha/status/1316578275360083969\">not all VCs are fans</a>).</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Second, it’s good for publishers. Broadcasting personal data also means broadcasting audience data. In turn, this leads to devalued audiences and lower revenue since the adtech companies in the RTB system can target high-value news audiences without paying news outlets. <a href=\"https://t.co/vqCmG9ydeS\">pic.twitter.com/vqCmG9ydeS</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; Robin Berjon (@robinberjon) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/robinberjon/status/1317104224443027461?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">October 16, 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></div>\n<p><strong>Update I: </strong>Responding to questions about next steps and the likely timeline for reaching a decision, a spokeswoman for the Belgian DPA told us: &#8220;In terms of procedure, now that the report of the Investigation Service has been transferred to the Litigation Chamber of the BE DPA, the Litigation Chamber will examine the case on the merits.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;At this time, we prefer not to provide an estimated timing for when the Litigation Chamber will reach a decision in this case,&#8221; she added.</p>\n<p><strong>Update II:</strong> Reached for her response to the report, the IAB Europe&#8217;s CEO, Townsend Feehan, told us the ad standards body would be issuing a statement in the coming hours. She also objected to the headline on this report, saying: &#8220;I find your headline to be misleading. It&#8217;s just factually incorrect.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Asked what is factually incorrect about it she objected to the phrasing &#8216;found to fail GDPR standard&#8217; &#8212; saying it &#8220;strongly suggests a ruling by an authority&#8221;.</p>\n<p>When we pointed out our reporting makes it clear the procedure is ongoing &#8212; including an explanation and a quotation from the Belgian DPA to that effect &#8212; she said: &#8220;The observation I would like to make is that I find your headline to be misleading and I believe it would be a more faithful representation of the truth if the headline could convey that a preliminary investigation finds [the TCF fails the GDPR standard].&#8221;</p>\n<p>On special category data she also claimed: &#8220;You can&#8217;t use the TCF to process special category data.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;I don&#8217;t want to go through the whole report with you but you put out a headline that gives the market the impression that the TCF has been found by a DPA to breach the GDPR and that is not the case,&#8221; she also told us, adding: &#8220;We will have a further statement on the way probably in the next couple of hours.&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Update III:</strong> You can now read the full IAB Europe&#8217;s statement on the findings of the Belgian DPA&#8217;s investigation <a href=\"https://iabeurope.eu/news-blog/iab-europe-comments-on-belgian-dpa-report/\">on its website</a>, where it writes: &#8220;The APD’s report represents the preliminary views of the APD’s investigations unit and has no binding effect with regard to any breach of the law by IAB Europe.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">Election Day approaches! Still not sure where the nearest polling place or ballot drop box is? Google wants to help.</span></p>\n<p>This morning the company rolled out a handful of features across <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/google\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"google\">Google <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> Assistant, Google Maps and Google Search, all meant to kick in when a user seems to be looking for information on voting locations.</p>\n<p>On Google Search, for example, a search for &#8220;ballot drop boxes near me&#8221; will now bring up a dedicated tool for finding just that — punch in the address where you&#8217;re registered to vote, and it&#8217;ll help you find a drop box or polling place accordingly. The same tool will also pop up when you search for things like &#8220;how to find polling place&#8221; or &#8220;where to vote,&#8221; so there&#8217;s some flexibility in it.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Or if you&#8217;ve got an Assistant-powered device nearby (like a Nest Mini, Nest Hub or an Android phone), you can say &#8220;Hey Google, where do I vote?&#8221; and Assistant should be able to figure it out accordingly based on your current location (with Assistant assuming, as it&#8217;ll note in its response, that your current location is where you&#8217;re registered to vote).</p>\n<p>The Maps integration is a bit more limited, but it gets the job done. Searching for &#8220;where do I vote&#8221; in the Google Maps mobile app results in a prompt that will toss you into the above web-based Google Search flow. Once you&#8217;ve found your location, tapping the &#8220;Directions&#8221; button will swing you back into the Maps app.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Fn5WAMnCY4\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/15/twitter-election-hub-voting-tools/\">Twitter debuts US election hub to help people navigate voting in 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Twitter debuts US election hub to help people navigate voting in 2020&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/15/twitter-election-hub-voting-tools/embed/#?secret=Fn5WAMnCY4\" data-secret=\"Fn5WAMnCY4\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Google says it&#8217;s pulling its polling location information from <a href=\"https://www.votinginfoproject.org\">the Voting Information Project</a> as part of a partnership with <a href=\"https://www.democracy.works/about\">Democracy Works</a>. The company says they&#8217;ll be adding more polling places leading up until Election Day, expecting to have more than 200,000 in the system when all is said and done.</p>\n<p>Don&#8217;t want to get your polling place details from Google, or just want to double check things? There&#8217;s always sites like <a href=\"https://www.vote.org\">Vote.org </a>(which, if you&#8217;re curious, is what Siri recommends when prompted with the &#8220;Where do I vote?&#8221; question), which also provides info on checking your voter registration status, becoming a poll worker, etc.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/2020-election/\"><img id=\"speakable-summary\">Last week The Exchange <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/09/funding-for-female-founders-falls-to-2017-levels-as-pandemic-shakes-up-the-vc-market/\">dug into recent data</a> concerning the amount of venture capital raised by female founders. As a refresher, the numbers were not good.</p>\n<p>In Q3 2020, <a href=\"https://pitchbook.com/news/articles/vc-funding-female-founders-drops-low\">PitchBook data</a> reported that US-based female founders raised $434 million across 136 rounds. That dollar amount was off from $841 million in Q2 2020, for context. The numbers were <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/12/09/us-vc-investment-in-female-founders-hits-all-time-high/\">a dramatic turnaround from where 2019 left the industry</a>.</p>\n<hr />\n<p><strong><em>The Exchange explores startups, markets and money. Read it <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/subscribe/?tpcc=theexchange\">every morning on Extra Crunch</a>, or get <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/newsletters\">The Exchange newsletter</a> every Saturday.</em></strong></p>\n<hr />\n<p>The sharp decline in available capital is slowing the pace at which women are founding new companies in the COVID-19 era. There are other factors at play, new data from the <a href=\"https://femalefounders.org/\">Female Founders Alliance</a> (FFA) indicates, but the funding drought is not helping.</p>\n<p>Overall, the pace at which women are indicating that they intend to found a company, according to a group of women that the FFA is tracking longitudinally, is slipping.</p>\n<p>FFA, a community of women founders and a startup accelerator working to achieve greater gender diversity in technology, built a sample of 150 women from tech hubs &#8220;with high likelihood of having entrepreneurial aspirations,&#8221; according to its dataset. It asked them about their entrepreneurial goals both before COVID-19 arrived, and again this September.</p>\n<p>The changes in responses from before the pandemic and today are striking. Let&#8217;s examine the data in light of what we learned last week concerning capital available for female founders and see what we can find out.</p>\n<h2>Depressing declines</h2>\n<p><div 10:29:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-17 10:29:49","title":"PearPop lets TikTok celebrities monetize by sharing shout-outs and screen time with fans","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2061973","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https://pearpop.com/\">PearPop</a> a new Los Angeles-based company, is on its way to racking up nearly 25,000 users in less than a month, and has already landed seed funding from the firm <a href=\"https://rocketonecapital.com/\">Rocket One Capital</a>.</p>\n<p>The company&#8217;s premise is simple. Allow fans to bid for shared screen time with their favorite <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/tiktok\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"tiktok\">TikTok <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> celebrities, and it&#8217;s one that has attracted the attention of a few of the platform&#8217;s stars with several million followers.</p>\n<p>The company was able to hook 3,000 users with one post from <a href=\"https://www.tiktok.com/@annabananaxdddd?lang=en\">Anna Shumate</a>, a TikTok star with 6.5 million followers who goes by the handle of &#8220;annabananaxdddd,&#8221; according to the company&#8217;s founder, Cole Mason.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>PearPop&#8217;s platform works by letting TikTok celebrities set a price for sharing screen time. They can accept bids and preview the content to approve to make sure it&#8217;s aligned with their persona on the platform. The payment is made through Stripe and the software verifies payment. Once paid, the celebrity posts the shared-screen video.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We built it for the influencer,&#8221; said Mason. &#8220;If you&#8217;re a fan trying to access your favorite TikTok star, then they can access them through PearPop instead of trying to contact a manager and pay for legal fees. You can simplify that and do that super easily.&#8221;</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2062051\" style=\"width: 292px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2062051\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"vertical wp-image-2062051\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_9860.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"282\" height=\"610\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_9860.jpeg 1242w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_9860.jpeg?resize=69,150 69w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_9860.jpeg?resize=139,300 139w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_9860.jpeg?resize=768,1662 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_9860.jpeg?resize=314,680 314w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_9860.jpeg?resize=710,1536 710w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_9860.jpeg?resize=946,2048 946w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_9860.jpeg?resize=23,50 23w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 282px) 100vw, 282px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2062051\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Promotional message from Anna Shumate for PearPop. <strong>Image Credit:</strong> <a href=\"https://pearpop.com/\">PearPop</a></p></div></p>\n<p>Mason thinks the company can rack up 100,000 users over the next three months and will head out to raise a seed round once he reaches that milestone. An Android and iOS version of the service is expected to launch in November, according to Mason</p>\n<p>The journey to founding PearPop began on the floor of an apartment in New York City. Mason was an aspiring model and serial entrepreneur who sold homemade wooden crosses door-to-door as a child and graduated to selling gloves for gamers in high school. Mason had moved to New York when he was signed to Ford Models.</p>\n<p>After sleeping on the floor of a friend&#8217;s apartment on St. Marks Place in Manhattan&#8217;s East Village, Mason tried to land modeling gigs but found more success as a promoter and manager of model apartments (places where young, pretty people can stay for free in exchange for making appearances at a few clubs around New York).</p>\n<p>&#8220;<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I hated it,&#8221; Mason said. &#8220;I always wanted to get into stuff in tech.&#8221; </span></p>\n<p>Mason took the cash from his promotion work and turned his attention to the tech industry soon after. As a struggling model who was building a network of friends in social media, he realized that the problem with the platform was breaking through.</p>\n<p>His initial solution was to build a platform called <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/gramenvy/\">GramEnvy</a>, which tried to find a way to growth hack Instagram.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The only way to grow your own Instagram was to have people post with you or about you and leverage their huge following.&#8221; Mason said. It was something easier said than done, and it was made harder by algorithmic changes that ultimately forced GramEnvy to close.</p>\n<p>But Mason was bitten by the entrepreneurial bug, and was inspired by the growing success of <a href=\"https://www.cameo.com/\">Cameo</a> to come up with another way that would enable popular minor celebrities on social media platforms (who were working a tier below the A-listers with tens of millions of followers) to monetize their performance on various platforms.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"xmum6SGu27\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/06/25/cameo/\">Cameo raises $50M to deliver personalized messages from celebrities &#038; influencers</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Cameo raises $50M to deliver personalized messages from celebrities &#038; influencers&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/06/25/cameo/embed/#?secret=xmum6SGu27\" data-secret=\"xmum6SGu27\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">And while Cameo is a way for celebrities to monetize their following, it doesn&#8217;t create the exposure that would-be social media stars are looking for. That&#8217;s the problem that Mason thinks he&#8217;s solved with PearPop. </span></p>\n<p>Other entrepreneurs, like Spencer Markel, the chairman of the Los Angeles-based children&#8217;s clothing and entertainment brand, CubCoats, thinks so too.</p>\n<p>Markel was introduced to Mason by a mutual friend from New York and has come on as an adviser to the company since Mason began working on it roughly 10 months ago. For Markel, the potential to actually share screens via TikTok&#8217;s platform makes PearPop a potentially more lucrative option for celebrities.</p>\n<p>&#8220;<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There’s a lot of different ways that this is going to address a gap in the market,&#8221; said Markel. He believes that the service should be a strong monetization opportunity for the TikTok stars who find themselves one level down from their higher-wattage peers with tens of millions of fans. </span></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"rBrb3IFX6I\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/06/15/you-can-set-up-a-zoom-call-with-tony-hawk-or-sinbad-using-cameos-latest-feature/\">You can set up a Zoom call with Tony Hawk or Sinbad using Cameo’s latest +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/IMG_9860.jpeg","linkMd5":"f3e009f11ea35068a16543e10c3e82e1","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn63@2020_1/2020/10/17/02-29-50-088_5540458694fe9e03.webp","destWidth":1242,"destHeight":2688,"sourceBytes":254522,"destBytes":85022,"author":"Jonathan 10:29:49","updatedTime":"2020-10-17 10:29:49","title":"Analogue takes on the TurboGrafx-16 with its Duo retro console","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2061962","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/analogue\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"analogue\">Analogue&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> beautiful, functional retro gaming consoles provide a sort of &#8220;archival quality&#8221; alternative to the cheap mini-consoles proliferating these days. The latest system to be resurrected by the company is the ill-fated, but still well-thought-of TurboGrafx-16 or PC Engine.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.analogue.co/duo/\">The Duo</a>, as Analogue&#8217;s device is called, is named after a later version of the TurboGrafx-16 that included its expensive CD-ROM add-on — and indeed the new Duo supports both game cards and CDs, provided they have survived all this time without getting scratched.</p>\n<p>Like the rest of Analogue&#8217;s consoles, and unlike the popular SNES and NES Classic Editions from <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/nintendo\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"nintendo\">Nintendo <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> (and indeed the new TurboGrafx-16 Mini), the Duo does not use emulation in any way. Instead, it&#8217;s a painstaking recreation of the original hardware, with tweaks to introduce modern conveniences like high-definition video, wireless controllers and improvements to reliability, and so on.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2061980\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-colors.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2061980\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2061980\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-colors.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"793\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-colors.jpg 2000w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-colors.jpg?resize=150,116 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-colors.jpg?resize=300,232 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-colors.jpg?resize=768,594 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-colors.jpg?resize=680,526 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-colors.jpg?resize=1536,1189 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-colors.jpg?resize=50,39 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2061980\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Analogue</p></div></p>\n<p>As a bonus, it&#8217;s all done in FPGA, which implies that this hardware is truly one of a kind in service of remaking the console accurately. Games should play exactly as they would have on the original hardware, down to the annoying glitches and slowdowns of that era of consoles.</p>\n<p>And what games! Well, actually, few of them ever reached the status of their competitors on Nintendo and Sega consoles here in the U.S., where the TurboGrafx-16 sold poorly. But titles like Bonk&#8217;s Adventure, Bomberman &#8217;93, Ninja Spirit, Splatterhouse and Devil&#8217;s Crush should be played more widely. Shmup fans like myself were spoiled with originals and arcade ports like R-Type and Blazing Lazers. The Ys series also got its start on the PC Engine (if you could afford the CD attachment). <a href=\"http://www.racketboy.com/retro/the-games-that-defined-the-turbografx-16\">Here&#8217;s a good retrospective</a>.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2061982\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-back.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2061982\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2061982\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-back.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"133\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-back.jpg 2000w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-back.jpg?resize=150,19 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-back.jpg?resize=300,39 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-back.jpg?resize=768,99 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-back.jpg?resize=680,88 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-back.jpg?resize=1536,199 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/turbografx-16-back.jpg?resize=50,6 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2061982\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">I wouldn&#8217;t mind having an HDMI port on the back of my SNES. Oh, Analogue makes one&#8230;</p></div></p>\n<p>Analogue&#8217;s consoles are made for collectors who would prefer not to have to baby their original hardware, or want to upscale the signal and play wirelessly without too much fuss. I still have my original SNES, but 240p just doesn&#8217;t look as crisp as it did on a 15-inch CRT in the &#8217;90s.</p>\n<p>At $199, it&#8217;s more expensive than finding one at a garage sale, but good luck with that. The original and its CD add-on cost a fortune, so if you think about it from that perspective, this is a real bargain. Analogue says limited quantities are available, and will be shipping in 2021.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"KVy7RE4xJr\"><p><a
